pattern — each API call fetches a fresh token instead of caching a potentially stale value\\n- `User-Agent` header on all outbound HTTP requests\\n- Wire Teams `clientInfo` timezone into the agent system prompt\\n\\n### AI UX Features\\n\\n- **AI-generated label**: All outbound messages include the `AIGeneratedContent` entity and `channelData.feedbackLoopEnabled` so Teams renders the \\\\\\\"AI generated\\\\\\\" badge and native thumbs up/down UI\\n- **Streaming responses** (1:1 only): Uses the [Teams `streaminfo` entity protocol](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoftteams/platform/bots/streaming-ux) with `onPartialReply` to progressively update messages as the LLM generates tokens, throttled at 1.5s via the shared `draft-stream-loop`\\n- **Informative status updates**: Sends a randomized status message (e.g. \\\\\\\"Scuttling through ideas...\\\\\\\") immediately when a message arrives, showing a blue progress bar while the LLM processes\\n- **Typing indicators**: Only sent in group chats (Teams doesn't support them in channels; 1:1 uses streaming instead)\\n- **Welcome card**: Sends an Adaptive Card with configurable prompt starters when the bot is added to a 1:1 chat\\n- **Feedback with reflective learning**: Handles `message/submitAction` invoke for thumbs up/down. Negative feedback triggers a fire-and-forget background reflection — the agent reviews its response, derives a learning, and proactively messages the user with adjustments. Feedback events persisted as `type: \\\\\\\"custom\\\\\\\"` / `event: \\\\\\\"feedback\\\\\\\"` in session JSONL for mining\\n\\n### Infrastructure\\n\\n- `updateActivity` REST helper and `updateActivity` on `MSTeamsTurnContext` for streaming\\n- `invokeResponse` handling — no-op in custom adapter (HTTP 200 sent by `process()`)\\n- Stream fallback for long replies (\\u003e4000 chars) — falls through to chunked delivery\\n- Stream finalization for empty text (clears progress bar when agent sends a card via tool)\\n- Shared `AI_GENERATED_ENTITY` constant extracted to `ai-entity.ts`\\n- New config fields: `welcomeCard`, `promptStarters`, `groupWelcomeCard`, `feedbackEnabled`, `feedbackReflection`, `feedbackReflectionCooldownMs`\\n\\n### Bug Fix\\n\\n- **Copy-pasted image downloads**: Added `smba.trafficmanager.net` to `DEFAULT_MEDIA_AUTH_HOST_ALLOWLIST` — pasted images arrive via Bot Framework attachment URLs at this host and require the bot's Bearer token, which was previously not sent because the host was missing from the auth allowlist\\n\\n### Known Issues\\n\\n- Proactive send from DM may route to wrong conversation when user has multiple conversations (#51947)\\n\\nCloses #51806\\n\\n## Manual test evidence\\n\\nTested on Azure VM deployment with Teams Web. 29/30 tests passed, 0 failed, 1 not tested (group chat). #51824\\n\\n## Problem\\n\\nWhen switching models in the Control UI, the model picker sends the **wrong provider prefix**. For example, selecting DeepSeek from a session running on ZAI produces `zai/deepseek-chat` instead of `deepseek/deepseek-chat` — causing \\\"model not allowed\\\" errors.\\n\\nThis is the root cause behind 9+ independent bug reports across different provider combinations (ZAI/DeepSeek, Ollama/Moonshot, MiniMax/Kimi, etc.).\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\nThree call sites use `resolveServerChatModelValue(model, modelProvider)` which blindly prepends the session's current provider to the bare model name:\\n\\n1. `ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts:542` — active session model display\\n2. `ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts:549` — default model display\\n3. `ui/src/ui/chat/slash-command-executor.ts:158` — /model slash command\\n\\nThe `modelProvider` from the server reflects the **previous** model's provider, not the newly selected model's provider.\\n\\n## User impact\\n\\nEvery user who switches between models from different providers in the Control UI gets \\\"model not allowed\\\" errors. Affects all multi-provider setups.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nFor bare model names (no `/`), create a raw `ChatModelOverride` and resolve the correct provider through `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue()`, which looks up the model in the catalog and returns the catalog's provider. Falls back to server-provided provider only if catalog lookup fails.\\n\\nAll 3 call sites are fixed. 2 files, +30/-7.\\n\\n## How to verify\\n\\n1. Configure 2+ providers (e.g. ZAI + DeepSeek)\\n2. Start a session with one provider's model\\n3. Switch to another provider's model via UI dropdown\\n4. Before: \\\"model not allowed\\\". After: switches correctly.\\n\\n## Tests\\n\\n`chat-model-ref.test.ts` covers `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue` catalog lookup. The fix routes through this existing tested path. No new test needed — the functions are correct, only the call sites were wrong.\\n\\n🤖 Generated with [Claude badge and native thumbs up/down UI\\n- **Streaming responses** (1:1 only): Uses the [Teams `streaminfo` entity protocol](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoftteams/platform/bots/streaming-ux) with `onPartialReply` to progressively update messages as the LLM generates tokens, throttled at 1.5s via the shared `draft-stream-loop`\\n- **Informative status updates**: Sends a randomized status message (e.g. \\\\\\u0026#34;Scuttling through ideas...\\\\\\u0026#34;) immediately when a message arrives, showing a blue progress bar while the LLM processes\\n- **Typing indicators**: Only sent in group chats (Teams doesn\\u0026#39;t support them in channels; 1:1 uses streaming instead)\\n- **Welcome card**: Sends an Adaptive Card with configurable prompt starters when the bot is added to a 1:1 chat\\n- **Feedback with reflective learning**: Handles `message/submitAction` invoke for thumbs up/down. Negative feedback triggers a fire-and-forget background reflection — the agent reviews its response, derives a learning, and proactively messages the user with adjustments. Feedback events persisted as `type: \\\\\\u0026#34;custom\\\\\\u0026#34;` / `event: \\\\\\u0026#34;feedback\\\\\\u0026#34;` in session JSONL for mining\\n\\n### Infrastructure\\n\\n- `updateActivity` REST helper and `updateActivity` on `MSTeamsTurnContext` for streaming\\n- `invokeResponse` handling — no-op in custom adapter (HTTP 200 sent by `process()`)\\n- Stream fallback for long replies (\\u0026gt;4000 chars) — falls through to chunked delivery\\n- Stream finalization for empty text (clears progress bar when agent sends a card via tool)\\n- Shared `AI_GENERATED_ENTITY` constant extracted to `ai-entity.ts`\\n- New config fields: `welcomeCard`, `promptStarters`, `groupWelcomeCard`, `feedbackEnabled`, `feedbackReflection`, `feedbackReflectionCooldownMs`\\n\\n### Bug Fix\\n\\n- **Copy-pasted image downloads**: Added `smba.trafficmanager.net` to `DEFAULT_MEDIA_AUTH_HOST_ALLOWLIST` — pasted images arrive via Bot Framework attachment URLs at this host and require the bot\\u0026#39;s Bearer token, which was previously not sent because the host was missing from the auth allowlist\\n\\n### Known Issues\\n\\n- Proactive send from DM may route to wrong conversation when user has multiple conversations (#51947)\\n\\nCloses #51806\\n\\n## Manual test evidence\\n\\nTested on Azure VM deployment with Teams Web. 29/30 tests passed, 0 failed, 1 not tested (group chat). {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_019hRhfoYwN8ScVvwgEBLTrD","type":"tool_result","content":[{"type":"text","text":"[{\"id\":4113940392,\"body\":\"## 🔒 Aisle Security Analysis\\n\\nWe found **2** potential security issue(s) in this PR:\\n\\n| # | Severity | Title |\\n|---|----------|-------|\\n| 1 | 🔵 Low | Prototype pollution via object spread in removePluginFromConfig when processing user-controlled config |\\n| 2 | 🔵 Low | Terminal escape/log injection via untrusted filesystem path in doctor notes |\\n\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 1. 🔵 Prototype pollution via object spread in removePluginFromConfig when processing user-controlled config\\n\\n| Property | Value |\\n|----------|-------|\\n| **Severity** | Low |\\n| **CWE** | [CWE-1321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1321.html) |\\n| **Location** | `src/plugins/uninstall.ts:77-161` |\\n\\n#### Description\\n\\n`removePluginFromConfig()` constructs new config objects using object spread over values derived from the on-disk config file (JSON5). If a malicious config contains a `__proto__` key (or similar special keys), spreading it into a new object can mutate the prototype of the created object, leading to prototype pollution.\\n\\nThis is now more reachable because the new Matrix “stale config cleanup” path calls `removePluginFromConfig(cfg,\\\"matrix\\\")` during `doctor`/install flows, which can execute on invalid-but-parseable configs.\\n\\nVulnerable code (object spread over untrusted object):\\n```ts\\nconst pluginsConfig = cfg.plugins ?? {};\\n...\\nconst newPlugins = {\\n  ...pluginsConfig,\\n  entries,\\n  installs,\\n  allow,\\n  load,\\n  slots,\\n};\\n...\\nconst config: OpenClawConfig = {\\n  ...cfg,\\n  plugins: Object.keys(cleanedPlugins).length \\u003e 0 ? cleanedPlugins : undefined,\\n};\\n```\\n\\nImpact depends on how polluted objects are later used, but typical risks include:\\n- Unexpected property lookups succeeding via polluted prototype (e.g., `if (obj.admin)` style checks)\\n- Crashes/DoS due to surprising inherited properties\\n- Bypassing logic that assumes plain objects\\n\\n#### Recommendation\\n\\nAvoid spreading/assigning untrusted objects into plain `{}` targets. Instead, create “plain” objects with a null prototype and copy only expected keys.\\n\\nExample fix:\\n```ts\\nfunction pickPluginsConfig(input: unknown) {\\n  const out: Record\\u003cstring, unknown\\u003e = Object.create(null);\\n  if (!input || typeof input !== \\\"object\\\") return out;\\n  const obj = input as Record\\u003cstring, unknown\\u003e;\\n\\n  ​// Copy only known-safe keys\\n  for (const key of [\\\"entries\\\", \\\"installs\\\", \\\"allow\\\", \\\"load\\\", \\\"slots\\\"]) {\\n    if (Object.prototype.hasOwnProperty.call(obj, key)) out[key] = obj[key];\\n  }\\n  return out as any;\\n}\\n\\nconst pluginsConfig = pickPluginsConfig(cfg.plugins);\\nconst newPlugins = Object.assign(Object.create(null), pluginsConfig, {\\n  entries,\\n  installs,\\n  allow,\\n  load,\\n  slots,\\n});\\n\\nconst config = Object.assign(Object.create(null), cfg, {\\n  plugins: Object.keys(cleanedPlugins).length \\u003e 0 ? cleanedPlugins : undefined,\\n});\\n```\\n\\nAdditionally, consider rejecting configs containing `__proto__`, `constructor`, or `prototype` keys during parsing/validation.\\n\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 2. 🔵 Terminal escape/log injection via untrusted filesystem path in doctor notes\\n\\n| Property | Value |\\n|----------|-------|\\n| **Severity** | Low |\\n| **CWE** | [CWE-117](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/117.html) |\\n| **Location** | `src/commands/doctor/providers/matrix.ts:106-112` |\\n\\n#### Description\\n\\n`cleanStaleMatrixPluginConfig()` builds a human-readable change message that includes `issue.path`, which ultimately comes from `cfg.plugins.installs.matrix` (config-controlled) via `detectPluginInstallPathIssue()`.\\n\\n- **Input (attacker-controlled):** `install.sourcePath` / `install.installPath` from config file\\n- **Propagation:** `detectPluginInstallPathIssue()` returns `path: candidatePath` without sanitization\\n- **Sink:** message is printed to the terminal using `note()` / `@​clack/prompts` with no escaping/neutralization of control characters\\n\\nAn attacker who can influence the config (or a synced/shared config) could embed control characters (e.g., ANSI escape sequences, newlines, carriage returns) in the path value. When `openclaw doctor` runs, the output could be manipulated to:\\n\\n- Spoof additional log lines / alter the appearance of warnings (log forging)\\n- Hide/overwrite terminal output (ANSI injection)\\n- Phish the operator by rendering deceptive prompts/commands\\n\\nVulnerable code:\\n```ts\\nchanges: [\\n  `Removed stale Matrix plugin references (${removed.join(\\\", \\\")}). ` +\\n    `The previous install path no longer exists: ${issue.path}`,\\n],\\n```\\n\\nand the note sink:\\n```ts\\nclackNote(wrapNoteMessage(message), stylePromptTitle(title));\\n```\\n\\nNo output neutralization is performed to remove control characters from interpolated values.\\n\\n#### Recommendation\\n\\nNeutralize control characters before writing untrusted values to terminal/log output.\\n\\nOptions:\\n\\n1) **Sanitize just the interpolated path** (recommended minimal fix):\\n```ts\\nfunction sanitizeForTerminal(value: string): string {\\n  ​// Strip C0/C1 control chars and ESC (\\\\u001b) used for ANSI sequences.\\n  return value.replace(/[\\\\u0000-\\\\u001F\\\\u007F-\\\\u009F\\\\u001B]/g, \\\"\\\");\\n}\\n\\n​// ...\\n`The previous install path no longer exists: ${sanitizeForTerminal(issue.path)}`\\n```\\n\\n2) **Centralize sanitization in `note()`** so all notes are protected:\\n```ts\\nexport function note(message: string, title?: string) {\\n  if (isSuppressedByEnv(process.env.OPENCLAW_SUPPRESS_NOTES)) return;\\n  const safe = message.replace(/[\\\\u0000-\\\\u001F\\\\u007F-\\\\u009F\\\\u001B]/g, \\\"\\\");\\n  clackNote(wrapNoteMessage(safe), stylePromptTitle(title));\\n}\\n```\\n\\nAlso consider shortening or redacting home directories (e.g., `~/...`) if doctor output is commonly shared in issue reports to reduce accidental path disclosure.\\n\\n\\n\\n---\\n*Analyzed PR: https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/53180 at commit `b91b344`*\\n\\n\\u003csub\\u003eLast updated on: If a malicious config contains a `__proto__` key (or similar special keys), spreading it into a new object can mutate the prototype of the created object, leading to prototype pollution.\\n\\nThis is now more reachable because the new Matrix “stale config cleanup” path calls `removePluginFromConfig(cfg,\\\"matrix\\\")` during `doctor`/install flows, which can execute on invalid-but-parseable configs.\\n\\nVulnerable code (object spread over untrusted object):\\n```ts\\nconst pluginsConfig = cfg.plugins ?? {};\\n...\\nconst newPlugins = {\\n  ...pluginsConfig,\\n  entries,\\n  installs,\\n  allow,\\n  load,\\n  slots,\\n};\\n...\\nconst config: OpenClawConfig = {\\n  ...cfg,\\n  plugins: Object.keys(cleanedPlugins).length \\u003e 0 ? cleanedPlugins : undefined,\\n};\\n```\\n\\nImpact depends on how polluted objects are later used, but typical risks include:\\n- Unexpected property lookups succeeding via polluted prototype (e.g., `if (obj.admin)` style checks)\\n- Crashes/DoS due to surprising inherited properties\\n- Bypassing logic that assumes plain objects\\n\\n#### Recommendation\\n\\nAvoid spreading/assigning untrusted objects into plain `{}` targets. Instead, create “plain” objects with a null prototype and copy only expected keys.\\n\\nExample fix:\\n```ts\\nfunction pickPluginsConfig(input: unknown) {\\n  const out: Record\\u003cstring, unknown\\u003e = Object.create(null);\\n  if (!input || typeof input !== \\\"object\\\") return out;\\n  const obj = input as Record\\u003cstring, unknown\\u003e;\\n\\n  ​// Copy only known-safe keys\\n  for (const key of [\\\"entries\\\", \\\"installs\\\", \\\"allow\\\", \\\"load\\\", \\\"slots\\\"]) {\\n    if (Object.prototype.hasOwnProperty.call(obj, key)) out[key] = obj[key];\\n  }\\n  return out as any;\\n}\\n\\nconst pluginsConfig = pickPluginsConfig(cfg.plugins);\\nconst newPlugins = Object.assign(Object.create(null), pluginsConfig, {\\n  entries,\\n  installs,\\n  allow,\\n  load,\\n  slots,\\n});\\n\\nconst config = Object.assign(Object.create(null), cfg, {\\n  plugins: Object.keys(cleanedPlugins).length \\u003e 0 ? cleanedPlugins : undefined,\\n});\\n```\\n\\nAdditionally, consider rejecting configs containing `__proto__`, `constructor`, or `prototype` keys during parsing/validation.\\n\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 2. 🔵 Terminal escape/log injection via untrusted filesystem path in doctor notes\\n\\n| Property | Value |\\n|----------|-------|\\n| **Severity** | Low |\\n| **CWE** | [CWE-117](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/117.html) |\\n| **Location** | `src/commands/doctor/providers/matrix.ts:106-112` |\\n\\n#### Description\\n\\n`cleanStaleMatrixPluginConfig()` builds a human-readable change message that includes `issue.path`, which ultimately comes from `cfg.plugins.installs.matrix` (config-controlled) via `detectPluginInstallPathIssue()`.\\n\\n- **Input (attacker-controlled):** `install.sourcePath` / `install.installPath` from config file\\n- **Propagation:** `detectPluginInstallPathIssue()` returns `path: candidatePath` without sanitization\\n- **Sink:** message is printed to the terminal using `note()` / `@​clack/prompts` with no escaping/neutralization of control characters\\n\\nAn attacker who can influence the config (or a synced/shared config) could embed control characters (e.g., ANSI escape sequences, newlines, carriage returns) in the path value. When `openclaw doctor` runs, the output could be manipulated to:\\n\\n- Spoof additional log lines / alter the appearance of warnings (log forging)\\n- Hide/overwrite terminal output (ANSI injection)\\n- Phish the operator by rendering deceptive prompts/commands\\n\\nVulnerable code:\\n```ts\\nchanges: [\\n  `Removed stale Matrix plugin references (${removed.join(\\\", \\\")}). ` +\\n    `The previous install path no longer exists: ${issue.path}`,\\n],\\n```\\n\\nand the note sink:\\n```ts\\nclackNote(wrapNoteMessage(message), stylePromptTitle(title));\\n```\\n\\nNo output neutralization is performed to remove control characters from interpolated values.\\n\\n#### Recommendation\\n\\nNeutralize control characters before writing untrusted values to terminal/log output.\\n\\nOptions:\\n\\n1) **Sanitize just the interpolated path** (recommended minimal fix):\\n```ts\\nfunction sanitizeForTerminal(value: string): string {\\n  ​// Strip C0/C1 control chars and ESC (\\\\u001b) used for ANSI sequences.\\n  return value.replace(/[\\\\u0000-\\\\u001F\\\\u007F-\\\\u009F\\\\u001B]/g, \\\"\\\");\\n}\\n\\n​// ...\\n`The previous install path no longer exists: ${sanitizeForTerminal(issue.path)}`\\n```\\n\\n2) **Centralize sanitization in `note()`** so all notes are protected:\\n```ts\\nexport function note(message: string, title?: string) {\\n  if (isSuppressedByEnv(process.env.OPENCLAW_SUPPRESS_NOTES)) return;\\n  const safe = message.replace(/[\\\\u0000-\\\\u001F\\\\u007F-\\\\u009F\\\\u001B]/g, \\\"\\\");\\n  clackNote(wrapNoteMessage(safe), stylePromptTitle(title));\\n}\\n```\\n\\nAlso consider shortening or redacting home directories (e.g., `~/...`) if doctor output is commonly shared in issue reports to reduce accidental path disclosure.\\n\\n\\n\\n---\\n*Analyzed PR: https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/53180 at commit `b91b344`*\\n\\n\\u003csub\\u003eLast updated on: token acquisition uses `app.getBotToken()` / `app.getAppGraphToken()`\\n- New `TeamsHttpStream` class (`streaming-message.ts`) implements progressive chunk delivery with sequence numbers and a shared `draft-stream-loop` throttle\\n- New `feedback-reflection.ts` module for fire-and-forget reflection on negative feedback with cooldown, session learning persistence, and proactive follow-up\\n- `monitor.ts` replaces `authorizeJWT(authConfig)` with a Bearer-prefix-only check — **inbound JWT signatures and issuer claims are no longer validated** (see inline comment); However, replacing `authorizeJWT(authConfig)` with a Bearer-prefix check removes the only mechanism that verified incoming activities were legitimately signed by Microsoft Bot Framework. The `adapter.process()` handler in `sdk.ts` does not perform inbound JWT validation either, so the security boundary is effectively gone. The new middleware only checks that the Authorization header starts with `\\\"Bearer \\\"` — it accepts any token string, including a random UUID.\\n\\nThe comment says \\\"The App registers its own JWT validation on POST /api/messages, so we delegate auth to the `adapter.process()` call\\\". However, `adapter.process()` in `sdk.ts` never validates the inbound JWT — it only calls `app.getBotToken()` to acquire an *outbound* token for sending replies. There is no inbound signature verification anywhere in the new code path.\\n\\nThis means any actor who can reach the webhook URL can send arbitrary bot activities by including `Authorization: Bearer \\u003canything\\u003e` in their request. To fix this, the `@microsoft/teams.apps` `App` instance should have its validation middleware mounted, or validation should be performed manually using Microsoft's OpenID Connect keys (e.g. `https://login.botframework.com/v1/.well-known/openidconfiguration`).\\n\\nHow can I resolve this? The fix replaces all three `resolveServerChatModelValue(model, modelProvider)` call sites with a catalog-lookup path (`createChatModelOverride` → `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue`) that resolves the correct provider from the model catalog.\\n\\n- **Root cause correctly identified and all 3 call sites patched** — `app-render.helpers.ts` (active session display, default model display) and `slash-command-executor.ts` (`/model` slash command).\\n- **Catalog lookup logic is sound** — `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue` handles ambiguous multi-provider matches and already has test coverage.\\n- **Unreachable fallback code** — in every patched site the `resolveServerChatModelValue` fallback is dead code for any non-empty model string. `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue` always returns a truthy value (either a qualified `provider/model` on catalog hit, or the bare model name on catalog miss), so the `if (normalized)` guard and the `||` branch are never false. On a catalog miss the callers now return a bare model name rather than the server-provided `provider/model` string that the comment promises. This is harmless in the common case but the comments are misleading and the fallback intent is not achieved.\\n\\n\\u003ch3\\u003eConfidence Score: 4/5\\u003c/h3\\u003e\\n\\n- Safe to merge; fixes a widespread provider-mismatch bug with correct catalog lookup logic, but the documented server-provider fallback is unreachable dead code in all three patched sites.\\n- The core fix is correct and well-scoped: catalog-based provider resolution replaces the stale session provider at all three call sites, directly resolving 9+ reported issues. The only concern is that the intended fallback (use server-provided provider when catalog fails) is structurally unreachable — `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue` always returns a non-empty string for valid input, so the fallback path returns bare model names on catalog misses instead of server-qualified strings. This is an edge-case behavioral difference on catalog-unavailable scenarios, not the main regression path, so it doesn't block merge.\\n- Both changed files share the same dead-fallback pattern; pay attention to `ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts` lines 544–552 and 563–570, and `ui/src/ui/chat/slash-command-executor.ts` line 161–162.\\n\\n\\u003c!-- greptile_other_comments_section --\\u003e\\n\\n\\u003cdetails\\u003e\\u003csummary\\u003ePrompt To Fix All With AI\\u003c/summary\\u003e\\n\\n`````markdown\\nThis is a comment left during a code review.\\nPath: ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts\\nLine: 544-552\\n\\nComment:\\n**Fallback to `resolveServerChatModelValue` is unreachable**\\n\\nThe guard on line 543 already asserts `activeRow.model.trim()` is truthy, so `createChatModelOverride(activeRow.model.trim())` will always return a non-null override. For any non-null, non-empty override, `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue` always returns a non-empty string — either a qualified `provider/model` from the catalog **or** the bare model name when the catalog has no match. Because `normalized` is always truthy here, the `if (normalized)` branch is always taken and the `resolveServerChatModelValue` fallback on line 552 is dead code.\\n\\nThe same unreachable fallback pattern exists in `resolveDefaultModelValue` (line 570) and in the ternary inside `slash-command-executor.ts` (line 162, the `||` branch).\\n\\nIn practice this means: when the catalog is empty or the model isn't listed, the functions now return a bare model name (e.g. `deepseek-chat`) rather than the server-provided `provider/model` string. That is arguably safer than returning a stale wrong-provider prefix, but it differs from what the `// Fallback: use server-provided provider if catalog lookup fails` comment promises, and could cause the model picker to show no matching option instead of the server's value.\\n\\nIf the intended behaviour is truly \\\"prefer catalog; fall back to server provider on catalog miss\\\", the check needs to distinguish \\\"catalog matched\\\" from \\\"bare name returned because catalog missed\\\":\\n\\n```ts\\nconst rawOverride = createChatModelOverride(activeRow.model.trim());\\nif (rawOverride) {\\n  const normalized = normalizeChatModelOverrideValue(rawOverride, state.chatModelCatalog ?? []);\\n  // Only trust the catalog result when it actually qualified the model.\\n  if (normalized \\u0026\\u0026 normalized.includes(\\\"/\\\")) {\\n    return normalized;\\n  }\\n}\\n// Fallback: use server-provided provider if catalog lookup fails.\\nreturn resolveServerChatModelValue(activeRow.model, activeRow.modelProvider);\\n```\\n\\nApply the same pattern to `resolveDefaultModelValue` and the `slash-command-executor.ts` ternary.\\n\\nHow can I resolve this?
